Defining Taqlid: The Layperson's Following
Sanusi defines taqlid with a concise technical phrase.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the precise technical definition of taqlid as the layperson's action based on a non-infallible mufti's statement.

Core Idea
Taqlid is not just following; it is following a non-infallible authority.

Sanusi begins by giving a concise definition of taqlid, emphasizing that it specifically involves a layperson following a mufti who is not infallible. This sets the stage for later discussions on the validity and limits of taqlid in Islamic theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic definition
Read the Arabic sentence slowly. Notice the key terms: taqlid, 'ammi (layperson), mufti, and the phrase 'laysa bi-ma'sum' (not infallible).
The definition is short but packed with meaning.
2
Understand the core idea
Sanusi defines taqlid as the layperson's action (ʿamal) by the statement of the mufti. Why does he specify 'action' and 'by the statement'? Reflect on the elements: the agent (layperson), the source (mufti's statement), and the nature (action/belief).
The phrase 'because he only believes and decides based on a non-infallible' explains the rationale.
3
Connect to broader kalam
Ask yourself: why is it important to define taqlid precisely? In kalam, taqlid is often opposed to independent reasoning (ijtihad). This definition highlights the need for valid evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
التقليدِ عمل العامّيّ بقولِ المفتي ؛ لأنَّهُ إنَّما اعتقد وجزمَ بقولِ مَنْ ليسَ بمعصوم (1) هو وتعريفُ ابنِ الحاجب للتقليدِ في «مختصره الأصلي » إِنَّما للغوي لا للاصطلاحي ، وقد اعتُرِضَ عليه بأنَّهُ ما كانَ اللائقُ بهِ إلا أن قصد يُفسِّر معناه الاصطلاحي ، وأمَّا غيرُ ذلكَ مِنْ معناه فناء عن تأليفه ، ولهذا لما أحسَّ ابنُ الحاجب بأنَّ إخراجَهُ مِنَ التقليدِ رجوعَ العامي إلى المفتي مخالف لاصطلاح جميع الأصوليين والفروعيين . . اعتذر عن ذلك آخر الكلام بقولِهِ : ( ولا مُشاحَّةَ في التسمية )(٢) لأنَّهُ فإِنْ قلتَ : يَرِدُ على حد الشيخ ابنِ عرفةَ أنَّه غيرُ منعكس ؛ يَخرج منه الاعتقاد الجازم بقولِ المعصوم : ( إِنَّ الله تعالى موجود ) مثلاً ونحو ذلكَ ممَّا لا يصح الاستناد فيه إلى مجرَّدِ الدليل السمعي . قلتُ : قد يُجابُ بأنَّ الحيثياتِ مراعاة في الحدود (٣) ، فيكونُ اعتقاد قولِ المعصومِ الذي يخرجُ مِنَ الحدِّ إِنَّما هو اعتقاد قولِهِ مِنْ حيثُ إِنَّهُ معصوم ، وذلك فرع عن معرفة دلالة المعجزة ، ومعرفة (١) انظر « المختصر الكلامي ) للإمام ابن عرفة ( ص ١١٠ ) . • (٢) انظر ( بيان المختصر » للعلامة الأصفهاني ( ٣/ ٣٥٠ ) (٣) بيَّن في هامش ( ح ) الحيثيات فقال : ( من حيث كونه معصوماً ، ومن حيث كونه غير معصوم ) ، فلا يكون المعصوم معصوماً إلا بإدراك المعجزة ، والمعجزة متوقفة على إثبات الصفات الله تعالى التي يتوقف عليها وجود ، ولا شك أنه وجوده تعالى منها ، فالعلم بوجوب وجوده تعالى متقدم عقلاً على خبر المعصوم . ١٤٩ ما يتوقَّفُ عليهِ مِنْ معرفةِ وجودِهِ تعالى ومعرفة صفاته تعالى التي لا تثبتُ دَلالة المعجزة إلا بعد معرفتها
Taqlid is the action of the layperson by the statement of the mufti, because he only believes and decides based on the statement of someone who is not infallible. And Ibn al-Hajib's definition of taqlid in his 'Mukhtasar al-Asli' is only linguistic, not technical. And it was objected to him that it was not fitting for him except that he intended to explain its technical meaning, and as for other than that from its meaning, it is extraneous to his work. And for this reason, when Ibn al-Hajib felt that his exclusion from taqlid of the layperson's return to the mufti contradicts the terminology of all usuliyyun and furu'iyyun, he apologized for that at the end of the speech with his saying: 'There is no quibbling over nomenclature.' So if you say: An objection arises against the definition of Shaykh Ibn 'Arafa that it is not reversible; there exits from it the firm belief in the statement of an infallible, such as 'God exists', and similar matters that cannot be based solely on scriptural evidence. I say: It may be answered that the aspects (al-haythiyyat) are taken into account in definitions. So the belief in the infallible's statement that exits from the definition is only belief in his statement from the aspect that he is infallible, and that is a branch of knowing the indication of the miracle, and knowing the miracle depends on establishing the attributes of God upon which His existence depends, and there is no doubt that His existence is among them. So knowledge of the necessity of His existence is prior rationally to the report of the infallible. That which it depends on from knowledge of His existence and knowledge of His attributes, which are not established except after knowing the indication of the miracle.
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage is a definition and defense of the technical definition of taqlid. It begins by giving a definition: taqlid is the layperson's action of following the mufti's statement, because he (the layperson) believes and decides based on someone who is not infallible. Then it critiques Ibn al-Hajib's definition in his 'Mukhtasar al-Asli', stating that his definition is merely linguistic, not technical. It was objected to Ibn al-Hajib that he should have explained the technical meaning; other meanings are irrelevant to his work. When Ibn al-Hajib realized that his exclusion of the layperson's recourse to the mufti from taqlid contradicts the terminology of all usuliyyun and furu'iyyun, he excused himself by saying 'there is no quibbling over nomenclature'. Then the passage presents an objection against Ibn 'Arafa's definition: it is not reversible, because it excludes firm belief in an infallible's statement (like 'God exists') which is based on rational evidence, not merely scriptural. The answer is that aspects (al-haythiyyat) are observed in definitions. The belief that exits is belief from the aspect of infallibility, which depends on knowing the indication of miracles, which itself depends on knowledge of God's existence and attributes—a rational process prior to accepting the infallible's report. Thus it is not pure taqlid.

Key Terms
تقليد
عامي
مفتي
معصوم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi's definition, who performs taqlid?
A) A scholar
B) A layperson
C) A mufti
D) An infallible

Key Takeaway
Taqlid is the layperson's adherence to a non-infallible mufti's statement, not any form of following.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you accept a fatwa from a scholar, do you feel a sense of certainty? Does this lesson challenge you to examine whether you treat that scholar as infallible? How will you adjust your attitude to acknowledge their fallibility while still following them with trust?
?
Have you ever felt that your belief in a religious ruling is unshakable because you heard it from a respected scholar? Reflect on the fact that the scholar is not infallible. How does that awareness affect your intellectual humility?
?
Consider a time when you followed a scholar's opinion without verifying from the Quran and Sunnah. This lesson shows that such following (taqlid) is valid for the layperson. But does it also remind you that the scholar is human? How can you balance trust with a realization that only Allah and His Prophet are infallible? Will you commit to seeking evidence when possible?

Critique of Ibn al-Hajib's Definition of Taqlid
Sanusi criticizes Ibn al-Hajib's definition as linguistic and rejects his apology.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Ibn al-Hajib's definition of taqlid was considered merely linguistic and how he responded to criticism.

Core Idea
Ibn al-Hajib's definition missed the technical meaning and relied on a verbal quibble.

Sanusi critiques a previous definition of taqlid by Ibn al-Hajib, pointing out that it is linguistic rather than technical. He explains the objection raised and Ibn al-Hajib's weak apology. This lesson highlights the importance of precise technical definitions in Islamic legal theory.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic text about Ibn al-Hajib's definition and the objection. Note the key phrase 'lughawi la li-l-istilahi'.
This distinction is crucial in Islamic sciences.
2
Identify the objection
The objection is that Ibn al-Hajib should have explained the technical meaning, not the linguistic one. Other meanings are irrelevant to his work.
Ibn al-Hajib's definition excluded the layperson's recourse to the mufti from taqlid.
3
Analyze the apology
Ibn al-Hajib's apology 'there is no quibbling over nomenclature' is seen as a weak excuse. Understand why this is insufficient.
The term 'mushahha' refers to petty arguing over terms.

Source Text

التقليدِ عمل العامّيّ بقولِ المفتي ؛ لأنَّهُ إنَّما اعتقد وجزمَ بقولِ مَنْ ليسَ بمعصوم (1) هو وتعريفُ ابنِ الحاجب للتقليدِ في «مختصره الأصلي » إِنَّما للغوي لا للاصطلاحي ، وقد اعتُرِضَ عليه بأنَّهُ ما كانَ اللائقُ بهِ إلا أن قصد يُفسِّر معناه الاصطلاحي ، وأمَّا غيرُ ذلكَ مِنْ معناه فناء عن تأليفه ، ولهذا لما أحسَّ ابنُ الحاجب بأنَّ إخراجَهُ مِنَ التقليدِ رجوعَ العامي إلى المفتي مخالف لاصطلاح جميع الأصوليين والفروعيين . . اعتذر عن ذلك آخر الكلام بقولِهِ : ( ولا مُشاحَّةَ في التسمية )(٢) لأنَّهُ فإِنْ قلتَ : يَرِدُ على حد الشيخ ابنِ عرفةَ أنَّه غيرُ منعكس ؛ يَخرج منه الاعتقاد الجازم بقولِ المعصوم : ( إِنَّ الله تعالى موجود ) مثلاً ونحو ذلكَ ممَّا لا يصح الاستناد فيه إلى مجرَّدِ الدليل السمعي . قلتُ : قد يُجابُ بأنَّ الحيثياتِ مراعاة في الحدود (٣) ، فيكونُ اعتقاد قولِ المعصومِ الذي يخرجُ مِنَ الحدِّ إِنَّما هو اعتقاد قولِهِ مِنْ حيثُ إِنَّهُ معصوم ، وذلك فرع عن معرفة دلالة المعجزة ، ومعرفة (١) انظر « المختصر الكلامي ) للإمام ابن عرفة ( ص ١١٠ ) . • (٢) انظر ( بيان المختصر » للعلامة الأصفهاني ( ٣/ ٣٥٠ ) (٣) بيَّن في هامش ( ح ) الحيثيات فقال : ( من حيث كونه معصوماً ، ومن حيث كونه غير معصوم ) ، فلا يكون المعصوم معصوماً إلا بإدراك المعجزة ، والمعجزة متوقفة على إثبات الصفات الله تعالى التي يتوقف عليها وجود ، ولا شك أنه وجوده تعالى منها ، فالعلم بوجوب وجوده تعالى متقدم عقلاً على خبر المعصوم . ١٤٩ ما يتوقَّفُ عليهِ مِنْ معرفةِ وجودِهِ تعالى ومعرفة صفاته تعالى التي لا تثبتُ دَلالة المعجزة إلا بعد معرفتها
Taqlid is the action of the layperson by the statement of the mufti, because he only believes and decides based on the statement of someone who is not infallible. And Ibn al-Hajib's definition of taqlid in his 'Mukhtasar al-Asli' is only linguistic, not technical. And it was objected to him that it was not fitting for him except that he intended to explain its technical meaning, and as for other than that from its meaning, it is extraneous to his work. And for this reason, when Ibn al-Hajib felt that his exclusion from taqlid of the layperson's return to the mufti contradicts the terminology of all usuliyyun and furu'iyyun, he apologized for that at the end of the speech with his saying: 'There is no quibbling over nomenclature.' So if you say: An objection arises against the definition of Shaykh Ibn 'Arafa that it is not reversible; there exits from it the firm belief in the statement of an infallible, such as 'God exists', and similar matters that cannot be based solely on scriptural evidence. I say: It may be answered that the aspects (al-haythiyyat) are taken into account in definitions. So the belief in the infallible's statement that exits from the definition is only belief in his statement from the aspect that he is infallible, and that is a branch of knowing the indication of the miracle, and knowing the miracle depends on establishing the attributes of God upon which His existence depends, and there is no doubt that His existence is among them. So knowledge of the necessity of His existence is prior rationally to the report of the infallible. That which it depends on from knowledge of His existence and knowledge of His attributes, which are not established except after knowing the indication of the miracle.
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage is a definition and defense of the technical definition of taqlid. It begins by giving a definition: taqlid is the layperson's action of following the mufti's statement, because he (the layperson) believes and decides based on someone who is not infallible. Then it critiques Ibn al-Hajib's definition in his 'Mukhtasar al-Asli', stating that his definition is merely linguistic, not technical. It was objected to Ibn al-Hajib that he should have explained the technical meaning; other meanings are irrelevant to his work. When Ibn al-Hajib realized that his exclusion of the layperson's recourse to the mufti from taqlid contradicts the terminology of all usuliyyun and furu'iyyun, he excused himself by saying 'there is no quibbling over nomenclature'. Then the passage presents an objection against Ibn 'Arafa's definition: it is not reversible, because it excludes firm belief in an infallible's statement (like 'God exists') which is based on rational evidence, not merely scriptural. The answer is that aspects (al-haythiyyat) are observed in definitions. The belief that exits is belief from the aspect of infallibility, which depends on knowing the indication of miracles, which itself depends on knowledge of God's existence and attributes—a rational process prior to accepting the infallible's report. Thus it is not pure taqlid.

Key Terms
تقليد
ابن الحاجب
مختصر الأصلي
لغوي
اصطلاحي
مشاحة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that any definition of taqlid is acceptable as long as it is consistent.
Correction: Sanusi shows that a proper technical definition is required; a linguistic definition misses the point and leads to contradictions.

Checkpoint
What was Ibn al-Hajib's definition of taqlid according to Sanusi?
A) Technical
B) Linguistic
C) Neither
D) Both

Key Takeaway
Ibn al-Hajib's linguistic definition and his apology were insufficient; technical precision is essential.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you learn a new Islamic concept, do you settle for the general linguistic meaning or do you push yourself to grasp the precise technical definition? What will change starting today?
?
Have you ever used the excuse 'there's no quibbling' to avoid correcting a flawed understanding? In what specific area of your deen will you commit to greater precision?
?
Ibn al-Hajib's weak apology allowed him to avoid addressing the contradiction. Where in your own life are you using 'no quibbling' as a shield instead of humbly accepting correction?

6 min
Objection to Ibn 'Arafa's Definition and Its Answer
Sanusi presents and answers an objection regarding the reversibility of Ibn 'Arafa's definition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objection that Ibn 'Arafa's definition of taqlid is not reversible, and how the concept of aspects (haythiyyat) resolves it.

Core Idea
Believing an infallible requires prior rational knowledge, so it is not taqlid.

This lesson presents a powerful objection to Ibn 'Arafa's definition of taqlid: it excludes belief in an infallible's statement (like 'God exists') which seems to be based on reason, not blind following. Sanusi answers by introducing the concept of aspects (haythiyyat), showing that such belief is from the aspect of infallibility, which itself depends on rational proofs.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Read the objection carefully: the definition is not reversible because it excludes firm belief in an infallible's statement like 'God exists', which is not based solely on scriptural evidence.
The objection uses the example of a clear rational truth reported by an infallible.
2
Understand the answer
Sanusi answers that aspects (haythiyyat) are considered in definitions. The belief that exits is from the aspect of the infallibility of the speaker, not from the aspect of the truth of the statement itself.
This is a subtle but critical distinction.
3
Trace the reasoning
The answer continues: belief in the infallible's statement from the aspect of infallibility depends on knowing the miracle (mu'jiza), which depends on knowing God's existence and attributes. Since rational knowledge of God precedes accepting the infallible's report, it is not pure taqlid.
This shows that even following an infallible involves rational steps.

Source Text

A) Because the infallible is a prophet

?

?
This lesson shows that even belief based on an infallible's statement involves prior rational steps. Do you ever assume that following a teacher or imam absolves you from personal intellectual responsibility? What one belief do you hold purely by taqlid that you could investigate rationally this week?
?
The concept of aspects (haythiyyat) protects definitions from appearing flawed. Are there areas in your own understanding of Islam where you dismiss a definition or ruling as inconsistent without considering the aspect from which it is applied? Write down one such case and re-examine it through the lens of aspects.

The Need for Reflection for Believers and Disbelievers
Sanusi answers an objection that only disbelievers need reflection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that reflection (fkr) is necessary for both disbelievers and believers, as it deepens faith and guards against doubts.

Core Idea
Reflection is not only for finding faith, but for strengthening it.

Some may think that once a person believes, reflection becomes unnecessary. This lesson examines that objection through a short dialogue. Sanusi shows that the same reasoning that makes reflection essential for the disbeliever applies equally to the believer, because reflection leads to knowledge and certainty.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how the objector states his case and how Sanusi responds with a question that leads to the objector's own admission.
The passage is structured as a dialogue.
2
Identify the objector's claim
The objector claims that only the disbeliever needs reflection. Find the exact phrasing and understand its implication: that the believer has no need.
3
Analyze Sanusi's response
Sanusi asks about the wisdom (hikmah) behind the disbeliever's need. The objector must admit that it leads to knowledge and faith. This reveals that reflection is for attaining knowledge, which is needed by believers too.
The response uses the objector's own logic to refute him.
4
Connect to the broader lesson
Reflection is an ongoing duty. Even after belief, it strengthens certainty and protects against doubts. This answers the objection fully.
Refer to earlier commands to reflect in the Quran.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا قالَ مَنْ لا معرفةَ لهُ بقواعدِ هذا الدين : إنَّما تمس الحاجة إلى الفكر للكافرِ الذي لم يؤمنٌ ، وأمَّا مَنْ آمَنَ وصدَّقَ فلا حاجة له إلى الفكر (٣)
فيُقال له : وما الحكمة في مسيس الحاجة للكافر إلى الفكر في المخلوقاتِ ؟ فلا بدَّ مِنْ أنْ يقول هذا القائل : ليطلعه فكره على العلم ، فيعرف الحق ويؤمنَ
And if one who has no knowledge of the principles of this religion says: "The need for reflection only applies to the disbeliever who has not believed; as for one who has believed and affirmed, he has no need for reflection" (3). It is said to him: "And what is the wisdom in the pressing need for the disbeliever to reflect on created things?" Then inevitably this speaker must say: "So that his reflection may lead him to knowledge, so that he may know the truth and believe."
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage presents an objection-and-answer structure. The objector argues that reflection (fkr) is only necessary for the disbeliever who has not yet believed; the believer already has faith and therefore has no need for reflection. The author responds by asking a question: what is the wisdom (hikmah) behind the disbeliever's need to reflect on created things? The objector must admit that the purpose is to reach knowledge, so that the disbeliever may know the truth and believe. The author's implicit point is that if reflection is beneficial for the disbeliever to attain knowledge and faith, it is also beneficial for the believer to strengthen his knowledge, increase certainty, and understand the evidence for his beliefs. Moreover, the Sharia commands reflection for all, as previously mentioned in the lesson about the commands to reflect in the Quran. This answers the objection by showing that reflection is not only for acquiring faith but also for confirming and deepening it.

Key Terms
فكر
حاجة
كافر
مؤمن
حكمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Once a person believes, reflection is no longer needed.
Correction: Reflection is a continuous duty that strengthens faith and guards against doubts, as seen in the Quranic commands to reflect.

Checkpoint
What does the author argue is the wisdom behind the disbeliever's need to reflect?
A) To impress others with his intelligence.
B) So that reflection leads him to knowledge and then to faith.
C) To argue with believers.
D) To find excuses for disbelief.

Key Takeaway
Reflection is not only for acquiring faith but also for confirming and deepening it, making it necessary for both disbelievers and believers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When was the last time you earnestly reflected on a single creation of Allah to strengthen your faith? If it has been a while, what does that say about your desire for knowledge of Him? Commit to reflecting on one thing today.
?
Do you ever find yourself acting like the objector, feeling that your faith is already secure and you don't need to think deeply? How does this attitude expose a lack of gratitude for the gift of reflection? Identify one area where you have stopped investigating.
?
If reflection leads to knowledge and faith, and you are a believer, why do you avoid deep contemplation? What are you afraid of losing? Choose a doubt you have and deliberately reflect on it using the Quran and creation this week.

Refuting the Claim that Nazar is Only for the Disbeliever
Sanusi refutes the objection that nazar is only for disbelievers and cites Quran 3:190.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why rational reflection (nazar) is not only for the disbeliever but essential for every believer to attain certainty and deeper understanding.

Core Idea
Reflection deepens faith; the one who reflects knows truth with proof.

Some claim that once a person believes, thinking is no longer needed. But this passage from Sanusi argues otherwise: if reflection leads a disbeliever to truth, how much more does it benefit the believer? The author uses a logical argument and a Quranic verse to show that contemplation is a sign of true understanding.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and response
Begin by reading the passage that presents the objection and Sanusi's response. Note how the author asks a follow-up question to expose the weakness in the objection.
2
Follow the logical argument
The author argues that if the disbeliever gains knowledge through reflection, then the one who reflects knows the truth along with its proof, making him more knowledgeable than one who accepts by imitation. Trace this logic step by step.
3
See how the Quran supports the point
The author cites Quran 3:190 praising those who contemplate the creation. Ask yourself: Does this verse describe disbelievers or believers? The rhetorical answer shows that contemplation is a trait of true believers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا قالَ مَنْ لا معرفةَ لهُ بقواعدِ هذا الدين : إنَّما تمس الحاجة إلى الفكر للكافرِ الذي لم يؤمن ، وأمَّا مَنْ آمَنَ وصدَّقَ فلا حاجة له إلى الفكر فيُقال له : وما الحكمة في مسيس الحاجة للكافر إلى الفكر في المخلوقاتِ ؟ فلا بدَّ مِنْ أنْ يقول هذا القائل : ليطلعه فكره على العلم ، فيعرف الحق ويؤمن . فإذا كانَ الأمر كذلكَ كانَ الكافرُ الذي نظر وعلم أعلم بالحقِّ ممَّنْ تلقَّى الإيمانَ بالقَبولِ ؛ لأنَّ الناظر عرفَ الحق ، وعرف طريقة وسبيله ، وبرهانه ودليله ، واتَّضحَتْ له دلالةُ صنعِ اللهِ تعالى ، فصار على يقين مِنْ دینِ اللهِ عزَّ وجلَّ ! وقد أثنى الله تعالى على مَنْ نظر في خلق السماواتِ والأرضِ ، وجعلَهم مِنْ أولي الألباب ؛ فقالَ : إِنَّ فِي خَلْقِ السَّمَوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضِ وَاخْتِلَافِ اللَّيْلِ وَالنَّهَارِ لَآيَاتٍ لِأُولِي الْأَلْبَابِ [آل عمران : ١٩٠] ، أَتُرَى هؤلاء هم الكافرونَ المعرضونَ عن آياتِ اللهِ تعالى ؟! كلا واللهِ ، إِنَّهم لهم العارفون بربهم من غير ريب في أمر خالقهم ، الذين نبههم القرآن فانتبهوا ، وأشار إليهم بالبرهان فتفطنوا ، وسارَتْ بهم مراكب الهدى ، حتى خرجوا مِنْ ظلماتِ الشكٍّ والرَّدى ، ونجوا مِنْ حبائل الرَّدى ، أولئك هم المهتدونَ، وَمَا يَجْحَدُ بِآيَاتِنَا إِلَّا الْكَفَرُونَ [العنكبوت : ٤٧] ، وإنَّما هو الهدى ثم زيادة الهدى ، ثم إتيان التقوى فالهدى الأول : هو العلم عن دليل مِنْ غير تقليد ، وزيادة الهدى : مطالعةُ خَرْقِ العوائدِ ، والتقوى : هي الفِرارُ بالقلبِ والجوارح
And if someone who has no knowledge of the principles of this religion says: 'The need for thought is only for the disbeliever who has not believed, but as for one who has believed and affirmed, he has no need for thought,' it is said to him: 'And what is the wisdom in the pressing need for thought for the disbeliever regarding created things?' So inevitably this speaker must say: 'So that his thought may lead him to knowledge, so that he may know the truth and believe.' If the matter is thus, then the disbeliever who reflected and knew is more knowledgeable of the truth than one who accepted faith by acceptance [without reflection]; because the one who reflected knew the truth, and knew its way and path, its proof and evidence, and the indication of the making of Allah Almighty became clear to him, so he became certain of the religion of Allah Almighty! And Allah Almighty praised those who reflect on the creation of the heavens and the earth and made them of people of understanding; He said: 'Indeed, in the creation of the heavens and the earth and the alternation of the night and day are signs for people of understanding' [Quran 3:190]. Do you think these are the disbelievers who turn away from the signs of Allah Almighty?! No by Allah, they are the knowers of their Lord without doubt about the matter of their Creator, those whom the Qur'an awakened so they woke up, and it pointed to them with proof so they became perceptive, and the ships of guidance sailed with them until they came out of the darkness of doubt and ruin, and were saved from the snares of ruin; those are the guided ones, 'And none reject Our signs except the disbelievers' [Quran 29:47]. Indeed, it is guidance, then increase of guidance, then bestowal of piety. So the first guidance: it is knowledge through evidence without imitation; and increase of guidance: contemplation of the breaking of norms; and piety: it is fleeing with the heart and limbs.
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an objection against the necessity of rational reflection (al-fikr) for the believer. The objector claims that thought is only needed for the disbeliever to reach faith; once a person believes, there is no further need. The author responds by first asking the objector to explain the purpose of thought for the disbeliever: it leads to knowledge and faith. Then the author argues that if the disbeliever gains knowledge of the truth through reflection, then the believer who also reflects will be even more knowledgeable, because he knows not only the truth but also its proof, its way, its evidence, and he sees the divine signs clearly, attaining certainty (al-yaqin). The author then cites Quran 3:190 praising those who contemplate the heavens and earth, calling them 'people of understanding' (ulu al-albab). The rhetorical question 'Do you think these are the disbelievers?' emphasizes that such contemplators are not disbelievers but true knowers who have been awakened by the Quran and guided by proof. They have emerged from doubt and ruin. The passage concludes by distinguishing three stages: first guidance (al-huda al-awwal) – knowledge through evidence without blind imitation (taqleed); increase of guidance (ziyadat al-huda) – contemplation of miraculous events (kharq al-awa'id); and piety (al-taqwa) – fleeing from sin with heart and limbs. Thus, rational reflection is not only for initial faith but also increases guidance and piety for the believer.

Key Terms
النظر
الفكر
اليقين
التقليد
أولو الألباب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Once someone believes, rational reflection is no longer needed.
Correction: This passage shows that even a believer needs nazar to gain certainty and deepen knowledge; the one who reflects knows the truth with proof, unlike the one who merely imitates.

Checkpoint
Why does the author claim that the disbeliever who reflects is more knowledgeable of the truth than a believer who accepts faith by imitation?
A) Because the disbeliever has witnessed miracles.
B) Because the one who reflects knows the proof and evidence of the truth.
C) Because the disbeliever is not a Muslim.
D) Because the believer has no need for knowledge.

Key Takeaway
Rational reflection (nazar) benefits both disbeliever and believer, but the believer gains deeper knowledge and certainty through it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you have certainty (yaqin) in your faith, or are you simply following what you were raised with? What concrete step will you take this week to reflect on a sign of Allah's creation to strengthen your certainty?
?
The passage says the reflective believer knows the truth and its proof. Can you articulate the proof for God's existence from your own reflection, or are you relying on others' arguments? If you cannot, will you commit to learning one proof from this lesson today?
?
When you read Quran 3:190 ('in the creation of the heavens and the earth... are signs for people of understanding'), does your heart stir with awe and drive you to contemplate? If not, what is preventing you from being among the 'people of understanding' that Allah praises?

The Three Stages of Guidance for the Believer
Sanusi clarifies the three stages of guidance that result from nazar for the believer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three stages of guidance that the believer attains through rational reflection: first guidance, increase of guidance, and piety.

Core Idea
Believers need nazar to increase in guidance and achieve piety.

In the previous part, Sanusi established that rational reflection is beneficial for all. Now, he elaborates on how the believer specifically benefits, describing three distinct stages: initial guidance through evidence, increase of guidance through contemplating miraculous events, and piety that leads to fleeing from sin. These stages show that reflection is not just for initial faith but for spiritual growth.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three stages
Read the short passage and note the three terms: al-huda, ziyadat al-huda, and al-taqwa. Understand what each refers to.
2
Define each stage
The author gives a definition for each: first guidance is knowledge from evidence without imitation; increase of guidance is contemplation of the breaking of norms (miracles); piety is fleeing with heart and limbs. Ponder how each depends on reflection.
3
Connect to the main argument
How does this three-stage description reinforce the necessity of nazar for the believer? Think about how each stage requires active intellectual engagement.

?

Responding to the Objection: Does Investigation Make the Unbeliever Superior?
Sanusi refutes the objection that an unbeliever who investigates knows more than a believing imitator.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi refutes the objection that an unbeliever who rationally investigates might know more than a believer who imitates, and how he uses Quranic evidence to affirm that the investigating believer is superior.

Core Idea
True knowledge comes from investigation, not blind acceptance.

Sanusi anticipates a powerful objection: If rational investigation (nazar) leads to certainty, then an unbeliever who investigates would have more certain knowledge than a believer who merely accepts faith by imitation (taqlid). This could make the unbeliever superior. Sanusi responds by turning the argument around: the believer who investigates is actually superior because he gains certainty through evidence. He supports this with the Quranic praise of those who reflect on creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage that begins with 'فإذا كانَ الأمر كذلكَ' through 'أولئك هم المهتدونَ'. Then read the translation. Notice the structure: a conditional statement, a claim about the unbeliever who investigates, and a Quranic support.
Pay attention to the rhetorical question: 'أثرى هؤلاء هم الكافرون؟'
2
Understand the objection
Sanusi is refuting an implicit objection: that if investigation is the source of knowledge, then an unbeliever who investigates might know more than a believer who imitates. The argument is that the investigator knows the truth and its proofs, so he is more certain.
3
Analyze the Quranic evidence
Sanusi cites Quran 3:190 which praises those who reflect on creation. He then asks rhetorically: are these the unbelievers? No, they are the knowers of their Lord. This shows that the one who investigates is not an unbeliever but a guided person.
The verse is used to show that reflection leads to guidance, not unbelief.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإذا كانَ الأمر كذلكَ كانَ الكافرُ الذي نظر وعلم أعلم بالحقِّ ممَّنْ تلقَّى الإيمانَ بالقَبولِ ؛ لأنَّ الناظر عرفَ الحق ، وعرف طريقة وسبيلة ، وبرهانه ودليله ، واتَّضحَتْ له دلالةُ صنعِ اللهِ تعالى ، فصار على يقين مِنْ دینِ اللهِ عزَّ وجلَّ ! وقد أثنى الله تعالى على مَنْ نظر في خلق السماواتِ والأرضِ ، وجعلَهم مِنْ أولي الألباب ؛ فقالَ : إِنَّ فِي خَلْقِ السَّمَوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضِ وَاخْتِلَافِ اللَّيْلِ وَالنَّهَارِ لَآيَاتٍ لِأُولِي الْأَلْبَبِ ﴾ [آل عمران : ١٩٠] ، أثرى هؤلاء هم الكافرونَ المعرضونَ عن آياتِ اللهِ تعالى ؟! كلا واللهِ ، إِنَّهم لهم العارفون بربهم من غير ريب في أمر خالقهم ، الذين نبههم القرآن فانتبهوا ، وأشار إليهم بالبرهان فتفطنوا ، وسارَتْ بهم مراكب الهدى ، حتى خرجوا مِنْ ظلماتِ الشكٍّ والرَّدى ، ونجوا مِنْ حبائل الرَّدى (١) ، أولئك هم المهتدونَ، وَمَا يَجْحَدُ بِآيَاتِنَا إِلَّا الْكَفَرُونَ (۱) [العنكبوت : ٤٧] ، وإنَّما هو الهدى ثم زيادة الهدى (٢) ، ثم إتيان التقوى فالهدى الأول : هو العلم عن دليل مِنْ غير تقليد ، وزيادة الهدى : مطالعةُ خَرْقِ العوائدِ ، والتقوى : هي الفِرارُ بالقلبِ والجوارح عمَّا يُبلغ إلى المخالفة لأمرِ الربوبية ، والانحطاط عن أوصاف العبودية إلى توهم الجبروتية ((١) .
الهوامش:
(1) الردى هنا : الموت ؛ يعني : على الضلالة ، والردى الأولى : بمعنى الجهل ، ومحيت من ( ح ) ، وكأنه قابلهما بالهديين الآتيين
(۲) في هامش ( ح ) عند قوله : ( هو ) : ( أي : الأمر والشأن )
(۳) ومثل له بقوله تعالى : ﴿ إِنَّهُمْ فِتْيَةٌ ءَامَنُوا بِرَبِّهِمْ وَزِدْنَهُمْ هُدًى ﴾ [الكهف : ١٣ ] ، فنظرهم إلى السماء وقولهم : لم يفعلها دقيانوس ، وإنما فعلها واحد عظيم . . هدى ، وكلام الكلب لهم وانخراق العوائد . . زيادة هدى
(۱) انظر « نكت الإرشاد ) ( ٤ ق ۱۹۱ - ۱۹۲ ) وزاد : ( والخوف من عذابه وصف المؤمنين ، والخوف من حجابه وصف العارفين ، والخوف من إعراضه تعالى وصف المحبين )
If the matter is so, then the unbeliever who investigated and knew would be more knowing of the truth than the one who received faith by acceptance; because the investigator knew the truth, and knew its way and path, its proof and evidence, and the indication of God's making became clear to him, so he became certain of the religion of God, the Almighty and Glorious! God Almighty praised those who reflect on the creation of the heavens and the earth, and made them of those possessed of intellect; He said: 'Indeed, in the creation of the heavens and the earth and the alternation of the night and the day are signs for those of understanding' [Al 'Imran 3:190]. Are these the unbelievers who turn away from God's signs? No, by God! They are indeed the knowers of their Lord without doubt in the matter of their Creator, whom the Qur'an awakened so they awoke, and whom it pointed to with proof so they understood, and the ships of guidance sailed with them until they came out from the darknesses of doubt and ruin, and were saved from the snares of ruin (1). Those are the guided ones, and 'None denies Our signs except the disbelievers' [Al-'Ankabut 29:47]. Rather it is guidance, then increase of guidance (2), then attainment of piety. So the first guidance is knowledge from proof without imitation; increase of guidance is witnessing the breaking of normal customs; and piety is fleeing with the heart and limbs from that which leads to opposition to the command of Lordship and descent from the descriptions of servitude to imagining sovereignty (1).
Footnotes:
(1) Al-rada here means death; i.e., upon misguidance; al-rada the first means ignorance, and it was erased from (H); as if he contrasted them with the two guidances to follow.
(2) In the margin of (H) regarding his saying 'huwa': 'i.e., the matter and affair'.
(3) And he gave as an example His saying: 'Indeed, they were youths who believed in their Lord, and We increased them in guidance' [Al-Kahf 18:13]. Their looking to the sky and their saying: 'Decianus did not do it; rather, a great one did it' is guidance; and the dog speaking to them and the breaking of customs is increase of guidance.
(1) See Nukat al-Irshad (4 q 191-192) and added: 'And fear of His punishment is the description of the believers; fear of His veil is the description of the knowers; fear of His turning away is the description of the lovers.'
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This passage is a defense of rational investigation (nazar) in acquiring true faith and a refutation of the objection that an unbeliever who investigates might know more than a believer who merely imitates. The author argues that if investigation leads to truth, then the believer who investigates is actually superior because he gains certainty through evidence and proof. He supports this with Quran 3:190, praising those who reflect, and clarifies that such people are not the rejecting unbelievers but rather those who are certain of their Lord. The passage then distinguishes three levels: first guidance (knowledge from proof without imitation), increased guidance (witnessing miraculous breaks in natural customs), and piety (fleeing from anything that leads to disobedience or imagining sovereignty in creation). The footnotes provide additional glosses, including the meaning of 'al-rada' as death or ignorance, and an example from the story of the People of the Cave where their reflection and witnessing miracles constituted guidance and increase of guidance.

تقليد
برهان
دليل
يقين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that if rational investigation leads to certainty, then an unbeliever who investigates would know more than a believer, making investigation harmful to faith.
Correction: Sanusi turns this around: the believer who investigates has the same knowledge plus the benefit of faith, and the Quran praises such reflection as a sign of true guidance.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what does the investigator gain that the imitator does not?
A) Certainty through proof and evidence
B) More reward from God
C) Avoidance of sin
D) Knowledge of the unseen

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
This passage says the investigator 'knows the truth, its path, its proof, and its evidence.' Do you know the proof for your own faith? If not, what is one specific step you can take this week to investigate it deeply?
?
Imagine you are that investigator who has gained certainty after reflection. How would your daily life, your prayers, and your relationship with God change? What is one thing you can do today to start living as if you have that certainty?

The Three Stages of Guidance: Knowledge, Miracles, and Piety
Sanusi enumerates three stages of guidance and defines each.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three distinct stages of guidance that Sanusi outlines: initial knowledge through proof, increased guidance through witnessing miraculous events, and piety as the ultimate goal.

Core Idea
Guidance is a progressive journey from proof to piety.

After establishing that the investigating believer is superior to the imitator, Sanusi refines the concept of guidance. He explains that guidance is not a single event but comprises three levels: the initial knowledge gained from proof without imitation, the increase of guidance that comes from witnessing the breaking of natural customs (miracles), and the piety that results from fleeing from disobedience. This passage provides a rich theology of spiritual development.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three levels
Read the passage from 'وإنَّما هو الهدى ثم زيادة الهدى' to the end. Underline the three terms: الهدى الأول, زيادة الهدى, and التقوى.
Note that the passage uses 'ثم' to sequence them.
2
Define each level
For each level, write its definition as given by Sanusi: first guidance is knowledge from proof, increase of guidance is witnessing the breaking of customs (miracles), and piety is fleeing from opposition to God's command.
3
Understand the relationship
Notice that these are cumulative: first guidance leads to increase, which leads to piety. Piety is the fruit of knowledge and witnessing miracles.
The footnotes give an example from the People of the Cave.

فإذا كانَ الأمر كذلكَ كانَ الكافرُ الذي نظر وعلم أعلم بالحقِّ ممَّنْ تلقَّى الإيمانَ بالقَبولِ ؛ لأنَّ الناظر عرفَ الحق ، وعرف طريقة وسبيلة ، وبرهانه ودليله ، واتَّضحَتْ له دلالةُ صنعِ اللهِ تعالى ، فصار على يقين مِنْ دینِ اللهِ عزَّ وجلَّ ! وقد أثنى الله تعالى على مَنْ نظر في خلق السماواتِ والأرضِ ، وجعلَهم مِنْ أولي الألباب ؛ فقالَ : إِنَّ فِي خَلْقِ السَّمَوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضِ وَاخْتِلَافِ اللَّيْلِ وَالنَّهَارِ لَآيَاتٍ لِأُولِي الْأَلْبَبِ ﴾ [آل عمران : ١٩٠] ، أثرى هؤلاء هم الكافرونَ المعرضونَ عن آياتِ اللهِ تعالى ؟! كلا واللهِ ، إِنَّهم لهم العارفون بربهم من غير ريب في أمر خالقهم ، الذين نبههم القرآن فانتبهوا ، وأشار إليهم بالبرهان فتفطنوا ، وسارَتْ بهم مراكب الهدى ، حتى خرجوا مِنْ ظلماتِ الشكٍّ والرَّدى ، ونجوا مِنْ حبائل الرَّدى (١) ، أولئك هم المهتدونَ، وَمَا يَجْحَدُ بِآيَاتِنَا إِلَّا الْكَفَرُونَ (۱) [العنكبوت : ٤٧] ، وإنَّما هو الهدى ثم زيادة الهدى (٢) ، ثم إتيان التقوى فالهدى الأول : هو العلم عن دليل مِنْ غير تقليد ، وزيادة الهدى : مطالعةُ خَرْقِ العوائدِ ، والتقوى : هي الفِرارُ بالقلبِ والجوارح عمَّا يُبلغ إلى المخالفة لأمرِ الربوبية ، والانحطاط عن أوصاف العبودية إلى توهم الجبروتية ((١) .
الهوامش:
(1) الردى هنا : الموت ؛ يعني : على الضلالة ، والردى الأولى : بمعنى الجهل ، ومحيت من ( ح ) ، وكأنه قابلهما بالهديين الآتيين
(۲) في هامش ( ح ) عند قوله : ( هو ) : ( أي : الأمر والشأن )
(۳) ومثل له بقوله تعالى : ﴿ إِنَّهُمْ فِتْيَةٌ ءَامَنُوا بِرَبِّهِمْ وَزِدْنَهُمْ هُدًى ﴾ [الكهف : ١٣ ] ، فنظرهم إلى السماء وقولهم : لم يفعلها دقيانوس ، وإنما فعلها واحد عظيم . . هدى ، وكلام الكلب لهم وانخراق العوائد . . زيادة هدى
(۱) انظر « نكت الإرشاد ) ( ٤ ق ۱۹۱ - ۱۹۲ ) وزاد : ( والخوف من عذابه وصف المؤمنين ، والخوف من حجابه وصف العارفين ، والخوف من إعراضه تعالى وصف المحبين )
If the matter is so, then the unbeliever who investigated and knew would be more knowing of the truth than the one who received faith by acceptance; because the investigator knew the truth, and knew its way and path, its proof and evidence, and the indication of God's making became clear to him, so he became certain of the religion of God, the Almighty and Glorious! God Almighty praised those who reflect on the creation of the heavens and the earth, and made them of those possessed of intellect; He said: 'Indeed, in the creation of the heavens and the earth and the alternation of the night and the day are signs for those of understanding' [Al 'Imran 3:190]. Are these the unbelievers who turn away from God's signs? No, by God! They are indeed the knowers of their Lord without doubt in the matter of their Creator, whom the Qur'an awakened so they awoke, and whom it pointed to with proof so they understood, and the ships of guidance sailed with them until they came out from the darknesses of doubt and ruin, and were saved from the snares of ruin (1). Those are the guided ones, and 'None denies Our signs except the disbelievers' [Al-'Ankabut 29:47]. Rather it is guidance, then increase of guidance (2), then attainment of piety. So the first guidance is knowledge from proof without imitation; increase of guidance is witnessing the breaking of normal customs; and piety is fleeing with the heart and limbs from that which leads to opposition to the command of Lordship and descent from the descriptions of servitude to imagining sovereignty (1).
Footnotes:
(1) Al-rada here means death; i.e., upon misguidance; al-rada the first means ignorance, and it was erased from (H); as if he contrasted them with the two guidances to follow.
(2) In the margin of (H) regarding his saying 'huwa': 'i.e., the matter and affair'.
(3) And he gave as an example His saying: 'Indeed, they were youths who believed in their Lord, and We increased them in guidance' [Al-Kahf 18:13]. Their looking to the sky and their saying: 'Decianus did not do it; rather, a great one did it' is guidance; and the dog speaking to them and the breaking of customs is increase of guidance.
(1) See Nukat al-Irshad (4 q 191-192) and added: 'And fear of His punishment is the description of the believers; fear of His veil is the description of the knowers; fear of His turning away is the description of the lovers.'
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This passage is a defense of rational investigation (nazar) in acquiring true faith and a refutation of the objection that an unbeliever who investigates might know more than a believer who merely imitates. The author argues that if investigation leads to truth, then the believer who investigates is actually superior because he gains certainty through evidence and proof. He supports this with Quran 3:190, praising those who reflect, and clarifies that such people are not the rejecting unbelievers but rather those who are certain of their Lord. The passage then distinguishes three levels: first guidance (knowledge from proof without imitation), increased guidance (witnessing miraculous breaks in natural customs), and piety (fleeing from anything that leads to disobedience or imagining sovereignty in creation). The footnotes provide additional glosses, including the meaning of 'al-rada' as death or ignorance, and an example from the story of the People of the Cave where their reflection and witnessing miracles constituted guidance and increase of guidance.

Key Terms
هدى
زيادة
خرق العوائد
تقوى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that guidance is just one event, or that miracles are the main source of faith.
Correction: Sanusi shows that guidance is a multi-stage process starting with rational proof, then miracles, then piety.

Checkpoint
What does 'increase of guidance' refer to according to Sanusi?
A) Learning more religious texts
B) Witnessing supernatural events that break natural laws
C) Performing many acts of worship
D) Teaching others

Key Takeaway
True guidance involves three stages: knowledge from proof, deepening through miracles, and culminating in piety.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Where in your life have you stopped at the first stage of guidance (knowledge from proof) without moving to the second stage (witnessing miracles) or the third (piety)? What is preventing you from deepening your faith through the signs of God?
?
Sanusi says piety is fleeing from anything that leads to opposing God's command. Is there an area in your life where you are holding onto something that subtly opposes God's command, claiming it's not that serious? Will you flee from it today?
?
The passage warns against 'descent from descriptions of servitude to imagining sovereignty.' Do you find yourself attributing power to your own efforts or to created things rather than recognizing God's sole sovereignty? How can you realign your heart this week?
